قبل أن يرتد إليك طرفك ﴾ [النمل: ٤٠] وأنه خلاف العادة فباعتبار التصور في الجملة انعقدت اليمين وباعتبار العجز الثابت عادة حنث للحال، وهذا العجز غير العجز المقارن لليمين لأن هذا العجز عن البر الواجب باليمين، وبهذا لا يتصور مقارناً لليمين، وإن كان في الكوز ماء وأهرق قبل الليل بطلت اليمين عندهما وعند أبي يوسف تبقى وتنعقد. والحاصل أنها إن كانت مطلقة وفيه ماء فما دام الحالف والمحلوف قائمين لا يحنث، وإذا هلك أحدهما يحنث غير أنه إن هلك المحلوف يحنث وقت الهلاك، وإن هلك الحالف يحنث في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياته لأن الحنث بفوات البر في جميع عمره وقد تحقق لوقوع اليأس عن الفعل. وإن كانت مؤقتة وإن كان الحالف والمحلوف عليه قائمين ومضى الوقت حنث في قولهم لوقوع اليأس عن الفعل في الوقت المشروط وإن هلك الحالف والمحلوف عليه قائم ومضى الوقت لا يحنث عندهم لأنه إنما يحنث في آخر جزء من أجزاء الوقت لأن شرط الحنث ترك الفعل في جميع أجزاء الوقت، فإذا كان للحال إن لم يكن فيه ماء وإن كان فيه ماء يحنث عند الصب. وأطلق المصنف في عدم حنثه في المسائل الثلاثة فشمل ما إذا علم الحالف أن فيه ماء أو لا، وما إذا علم أن لا ماء فيه . وقيده الأسبيجابي بعدم علمه بأن لا ماء فيه، وأما إذا علم بأن لا ماء فيه يحنث بالاتفاق ا هـ . لأنه إذا علم وقعت يمينه على ما يخلق الله تعالى فيه وقد تحقق العدم فيحنث، وروي عن أبي حنيفة في رواية أخرى أنه قال : لا يحنث علم أو لم يعلم وهو قول زفر ا هـ. وصحح في التبيين هذه الرواية في شرح قوله إن لم أقتل فلاناً فكذا، ولذا أطلق هنا في المختصر وجزم بالإطلاق في فتح القدير . وقد تفرع على هذا الأصل مسائل منها ما لو حلف ليقتلن زيداً اليوم فمات زيد قبل مضي اليوم لا يحنث عندهما كما سيأتي بيانه. ومنها لو حلف ليأكلن هذا الرغيف اليوم فأكله غيره قبل الليل. ومنها لو حلف ليقضين فلاناً دينه غداً عندهما. ومنها لو حلف لا يعطيه حتى يأذن فلان فمات فلان ثم أعطاه لم يحنث، وكذا ولا ميتاً في آخر الوقت فالميت لا يوصف بالحنث . ولو هلك المحلوف عليه والوقت باق والحالف قائم بطلت اليمين عندهما وعند أبي البر وقد فات لكن ذكر في الجوهرة في شرح صعود السماء وقلب الحجر ذهباً أن المؤقتة يتعلق انعقادها بآخر الوقت عندهما . يعني ومحمداً فإذا كان كذلك فقوله «لم تنعقد صحيح في الكل، والذي يظهر من كلامهم أن في المسألة
Book of Oaths, Chapter on Oaths Regarding Eating, Drinking, Clothing, and Speech. For the expiation, and there is no difference on this disagreement between an oath by Allah the Exalted or by divorce, and for this reason he [the author] exemplified it in al-Mukhtasar with an oath of divorce or manumission. The author has mentioned the issue of the pitcher, which is derived from this principle, and he stated that it has four aspects: two aspects in the restricted [time-bound] and two aspects in the absolute. As for the restricted, it has two aspects: either there is no water in it at all, or there was water at the time of the oath and then it was poured before the time elapsed—in each of them he does not become sinful due to the non-formation of the oath in the first and its invalidation upon pouring in the second according to them [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad]. There is no difference in the time whether it is a day, a month, or a week. As for the absolute, it has two aspects: either there is water in it at all—he does not become sinful due to the non-formation of the oath; or there was water and he poured, then he becomes sinful because the oath is formed due to the possibility of fulfillment, then he becomes sinful upon pouring because fulfillment became obligatory upon him as soon as he finished, so when he pours, fulfillment is lost, so he becomes sinful at that time, just as if the oath-taker dies while the water remains. The apparent meaning of their statement is that there is no difference between his pouring it himself or someone else, or the pitcher tilting and its contents pouring out without any action. As for Abu Yusuf, he becomes sinful in all aspects, except that in the time-bound he becomes sinful at the end of the time, and in the absolute he becomes sinful immediately if there is no water; if there is water, he becomes sinful upon pouring. The author gave an absolute ruling of non-sin in the three cases, which includes whether the oath-taker knew that there was water in it or not, and whether he knew that there was no water in it. Al-Asbijabi restricted it to his not knowing that there was no water in it; but if he knows that there is no water in it, he becomes sinful by consensus. This is because if he knows, his oath is upon what Allah creates in it, and non-existence has been realized, so he becomes sinful. It is narrated from Abu Hanifa in another narration that he said: He does not become sinful whether he knows or not, and this is the saying of Zufar. Al-Tabyin authenticated this narration in the explanation of his saying 'if I do not kill so-and-so, then such-and-such', and for this reason he gave an absolute ruling here in al-Mukhtasar and asserted the absolute ruling in Fath al-Qadir. Based on this principle, there are branched issues, including: if he swore to kill Zayd today and Zayd died before the day passed, he does not become sinful according to them as will be explained; including if he swore to eat this loaf of bread today and someone else ate it before nightfall; including if he swore to pay so-and-so his debt tomorrow and so-and-so had died without his knowledge, or one of them died before tomorrow passed, or he paid it before, or so-and-so discharged him before, the oath does not take effect; including if he said to Zayd, 'If I see Amr and do not inform you, my slave is free,' and he saw him with Zayd and remained silent and did not say anything, or he said 'He is Amr,' the slave is freed according to them; including if he swore not to give him until so-and-so permits, and so-and-so died, then he gave him, he does not become sinful; similarly, if he dies at the end of the time, the dead person cannot be described as sinful. If the object of the oath perishes while the time remains and the oath-taker is alive, the oath is invalid according to them, while according to Abu Yusuf he becomes sinful. End of summary. His saying: 'And the author gave an absolute ruling'—al-Ramli said: The implication of what he chose in the issue of 'if I do not kill so-and-so' regarding the detail between knowledge and ignorance is that his absolute ruling here should be interpreted as referring to ignorance, to apply the absolute to the restricted so that it follows a single pattern, even though in al-Tabyin he authenticated the narration of the absolute ruling, possibly because he chose the detailed narration like al-Asbijabi, so there is a difference in authentication and preference in the issue, as is apparent. However, al-Zaylai distinguished between the issue of the pitcher and the issue of killing: because if he is knowledgeable, he has contracted his oath upon a life that Allah creates, which is conceivable, unlike the issue of the pitcher, since what Allah creates in it is not the object of the oath. Therefore, what he gave as an absolute here follows its absolute meaning. Consider. That is because the object of the oath here is water contained in the pitcher at the time of the oath, not what occurs later. But it could be said that if he knows there is no water in it, the intended meaning is water that will be contained in it after the oath, as in 'I will kill so-and-so'—killing is the removal of life, so if he knows he is dead, the intended meaning is a newly created soul. His saying: 'does not take effect'—al-Ramli said: The non-formation applies when he is dead at the time of the oath; but if one of them dies before the passing of the morrow, or he pays it before, or he discharges him before, it becomes invalid after formation, since the condition for the continuation of the time-bound oath is the possibility of fulfillment, and it has ceased. However, it is mentioned in al-Jawhara in the explanation of ascending to heaven and turning stone into gold that the time-bound oath's formation is related to the end of the time according to them [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad]. So if that is the case, his statement 'does not take effect' is correct in all. What appears from their statements is that there are two sayings: some say invalidation after formation, some say non-formation except at the end of the time. Consider. His saying: 'including if he swore not to give him until so-and-so permits'—so-and-so is without restriction to a day in the copies, and it is like that in al-Fath. Consider the issue of Abu Hanifa. The issue.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the ruling of oaths that involve impossible acts, using the example of an oath to drink from a pitcher (الكوز). The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq, following the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, explains that an oath to do something impossible does not come into effect (لا تنعقد) because the very purpose of an oath—to affirm the truth of a matter by vowing to fulfill a specific action—is thwarted when fulfillment is impossible. He classifies the ruling into four scenarios: two for time-bound (مقيدة) oaths and two for absolute (مطلقة) oaths. For a time-bound oath, if the pitcher has no water at all at the time of the oath, the oath never takes effect; if it had water but the water is poured before the time expires, the oath becomes void upon pouring according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). For an absolute oath, if there is no water at all, the oath does not take effect; if there is water and the person pours it, the oath was valid at inception (since fulfillment was possible) but becomes violated upon pouring, triggering sin and expiation. The text notes that Abu Yusuf differs: he holds that in all these cases the oath is valid and the person becomes sinful, except that in time-bound oaths the sin occurs at the end of the time, not at the time of pouring. The passage then delves into the rationale: the oath's validity depends on the possibility of 'birr' (obedience/fulfillment). If the action is inherently impossible (like drinking from a pitcher with no water), there is no subject (معقود عليه) and the oath is void like a false oath (يمين غموس). However, for actions that are merely unusual (like ascending to heaven or turning stone to gold), the oath is valid because such things are conceivable for Allah even if not normally possible—thus the person becomes sinful immediately due to his inability in the usual course. The later commentary discusses whether the oath-taker's knowledge of impossibility matters: al-Asbijabi restricts the voidness to cases of ignorance; if the person knows there is no water, he is sinful by consensus (since his oath is then on an impossible thing knowingly). Another narration from Abu Hanifa (supported by Zufar) says no sin even if he knows, and al-Tabyin prefers this absolute view, though other scholars like al-Ramli and al-Zaylai try to harmonize or distinguish between cases. The passage concludes with several derived rulings (furū‘āt) applying the same principle: e.g., swearing to kill someone who is already dead, to eat bread that someone else eats, to pay a debt to a dead person, etc.

Key Terms
الكوز (al-kūz): The pitcher used as an example in the oath; its content (water) is the subject of the oath.
انعقاد اليمين (in‘iqād al-yamīn): The coming into effect of the oath; a valid oath that creates a legal obligation to fulfill or expiate.
العلم (al-‘ilm): Knowledge; in this context, the swearer's awareness of the impossibility of the act affects the ruling.
الفرع (al-far‘): Branched issue; derived case applying the same principle to different facts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi authorities (al-Asbijabi), what is the ruling for an oath to do an impossible act if the swearer was unaware of the impossibility?
A) The oath is valid and sin occurs.
B) The oath does not take effect and no sin.
C) The oath is void but sin occurs due to ignorance.
D) The oath is valid but no sin because of ignorance.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has diverse positions on oaths involving impossible acts; the mufta bihi today considers the swearer's knowledge and typically follows the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Oath on Water in a Jug: The Effect of Knowledge
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of knowledge in an oath regarding a jug's contents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on an oath to drink from a jug when the swearer knows it is empty, and identify the two narrations from Abu Hanifa and the preferred view.

Core Idea
Knowledge of emptiness does not break an oath on water in a jug because the oath is on the existing water, not future creation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks an apparent contradiction in Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The matn states an unqualified ruling that an oath to drink from a jug is not broken even if the jug is empty. Yet a different case—an oath to kill a dead person—seems to suggest that knowledge matters. How do Hanafi commentators reconcile these? This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and the reasoning behind the preferred position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling of the matn
The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that an oath to drink from a jug is not broken if there is no water, and broken if there is water and the swearer pours it. The author gave an unqualified statement of non-breach in three issues.
The 'three issues' likely include the case where the jug is empty, where the swearer is ignorant, etc.
2
Locate the ikhtilaf
Al-Asbajabi restricted this: if the swearer knows there is no water, he breaks the oath by consensus. But another narration from Abu Hanifa and Zufar says no breach regardless.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the other narration is considered nawadir.
3
Examine the reasoning (ta'lil)
The reasoning for the distinction in the killing case: the oath is on a life created by Allah. In the jug case, the water is already existent, so knowledge is irrelevant.
Al-Zayla'i's distinction is key to understanding the preferred position.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
Al-Tabyin preferred the unqualified narration; al-Zayla'i distinguished the two cases to support this preference. The mufta bihi is that the oath is not broken.
This is the position in al-Mukhtasar and Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الأيمان باب اليمين في الأكل والشرب واللبس والكلام للحال إن لم يكن فيه ماء وإن كان فيه ماء يحنث عند الصب. وأطلق المصنف في عدم حنثه في المسائل الثلاثة فشمل ما إذا علم الحالف أن فيه ماء أو لا، وما إذا علم أن لا ماء فيه . وقيده الأسبيجابي بعدم علمه بأن لا ماء فيه، وأما إذا علم بأن لا ماء فيه يحنث بالاتفاق ا هـ . لأنه إذا علم وقعت يمينه على ما يخلق الله تعالى فيه وقد تحقق العدم فيحنث، وروي عن أبي حنيفة في رواية أخرى أنه قال : لا يحنث علم أو لم يعلم وهو قول زفر ا هـ. وصحح في التبيين هذه الرواية في شرح قوله إن لم أقتل فلاناً فكذا، ولذا أطلق هنا في المختصر وجزم بالإطلاق في فتح القدير .
قوله : (وأطلق المصنف الخ) قال الرملي : مقتضى ما اختاره في مسألة إن لم أقتل فلاناً من التفصيل بين العلم وعدمه أن يحمل إطلاقه هنا على عدم العلم حملاً للمطلق على المقيد ليكن ماشياً على وتيرة واحدة وإن كان في التبيين صحح رواية الإطلاق لاحتمال اختياره رواية التفصيل كالأسبيجابي فيكون في المسألة اختلاف التصحيح والترجيح كما هو ظاهر لكن الزيلعي فرق بين مسألة الكوز وبين مسألة القتل بأنه إذا كان عالماً فقد عقد يمينه على حياة يحدثها الله تعالى وهو متصور بخلاف مسألة الكوز فإن ما يحدثه الله تعالى فيه غير المحلوف عليه فيكون ما أطلقه هنا جارياً على إطلاقه تأمل ا هـ . أي لأن المحلوف عليه هنا ماء مظروف في الكوز وقت الحلف دون الحادث بعده
Chapter of Oaths, Section on Oaths concerning Eating, Drinking, Wearing, and Speaking. For the present state, if there is no water in it, and if there is water in it, he breaks the oath upon pouring. And the author gave an unqualified ruling of non-breach in the three issues, so it includes the case where the swearer knows there is water or not, and the case where he knows there is no water. Al-Asbajabi restricted it to his ignorance of there being no water; but if he knows there is no water, he breaks the oath by consensus. Because if he knows, his oath falls on what Allah creates in it and non-existence is realized, so he breaks it. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa in another narration that he said: He does not break the oath, whether he knows or does not know, and that is the statement of Zufar. And al-Tabyin authenticated this narration in the commentary on his statement 'If I did not kill so-and-so...', and therefore he gave an unqualified ruling here in al-Mukhtasar and confirmed the unqualified ruling in Fath al-Qadir. Then he said: Qawluh (his statement): 'And the author gave an unqualified ruling...' Al-Ramli said: The implication of his choice in the issue of 'If I did not kill so-and-so' of the distinction between knowledge and ignorance is that his unqualified statement here should be interpreted as referring to ignorance, carrying the absolute to the restricted so that it is consistent. Even if al-Tabyin authenticated the narration of the unqualified ruling, due to the possibility that he chose the narration of the distinction like al-Asbajabi, so there is a difference in authentication and preference in the issue, as is apparent. But al-Zayla'i distinguished between the issue of the jug and the issue of killing: if he knows, he has based his oath on a life that Allah creates, which is conceivable, unlike the issue of the jug, because what Allah creates in it is not the subject of the oath. Thus what he gave unqualifiedly here is to be taken as unqualified. Tammal (reflect). End. That is because the subject of the oath here is water contained in the jug at the time of the oath, not what occurs afterwards.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It presents a ruling on an oath to drink from a jug, focusing on the condition of knowledge. The author initially states that if the jug contains no water at the time of the oath, the swearer does not break his oath; but if it contains water and he pours it out, he breaks it. However, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about whether the swearer's knowledge of the water's absence affects this ruling. The main text (of Kanz) gives an unqualified statement that he does not break his oath in these three issues (including when there is water but he doesn't know, etc.). Al-Asbajabi qualified it: if the swearer knows there is no water, he breaks his oath by consensus; but if he is ignorant, he does not. Another narration from Abu Hanifa, also held by Zufar, says he does not break his oath regardless of knowledge. Al-Tabyin (a commentary) preferred the latter narration. The commentary then discusses the tension between this case and the case of an oath to kill a dead person, where knowledge matters. Al-Zayla'i reconciles: in the killing case, the oath is on a future life created by Allah, which is conceivable if he knows the person is dead? Actually the reasoning is that the oath is on something that could be created, whereas in the jug case, the water is already in the jug at the time of the oath, not something to be created later. So the unqualified ruling is appropriate.

Key Terms
حنث (hanith): Breaking an oath, i.e., the state where the swearer has violated his oath and becomes liable for expiation (kaffarah).
كوز (kuz): A jug or vessel; in this context, it refers to a container that may or may not contain water.
علم (ilm): Knowledge; specifically, the swearer's knowledge of the actual state of the subject of the oath at the time of swearing.
إطلاق (itlaq): Unqualified or absolute statement; here, the author's unqualified ruling without conditioning on knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Zayla'i's distinction, why does the oath on a jug not require consideration of knowledge, unlike the oath to kill a dead person?
A) Because the jug case involves an existing object, while the killing case involves a future event that Allah may create.
B) Because the jug case involves an oath on a drink, which is less serious.
C) Because the killing case is haram, so knowledge matters more.
D) Because al-Asbajabi's view is weaker in transmission.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi preferred position (mufta bihi) for an oath to drink from a jug that is empty is that the oath is not broken, regardless of the swearer's knowledge, because the oath is on the existing subject.

Oath Void vs Broken When Subject Perishes
List of derivative cases applying the principle of oath on a non-existent subject

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a temporal oath when the subject perishes before the time ends, and distinguish the positions of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) from Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
If the subject of a temporal oath perishes before the deadline, the oath is void — not broken — according to the majority of the Hanafi school.

In the previous lesson, we established the principle that an oath on a non-existent subject is not contracted. This lesson expands by examining cases where the subject exists at the time of the oath but ceases to exist before the time expires. The key question: does the oath become void (batil) or is it broken (hanth)? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer, with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad holding one view and Abu Yusuf another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of oath (temporal)
Determine that the oath is restricted to a specific time period, such as 'today' or 'tonight'.
The term used in the text is 'yamin muwaqqata'.
2
Note the timeline: subject exists at oath, perishes within the time
The subject of the oath (e.g., Zayd, the loaf) is present when the swearer makes the oath, but dies or is destroyed before the specified time ends.
The swearer remains alive throughout.
3
Recognize the two positions
According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the oath is void (tabtul al-yamin) and no kaffarah is due. According to Abu Yusuf, the oath is broken (yahnuth) and kaffarah is required.
The text states: 'batalat al-yamin 'indahuma wa 'inda Abi Yusuf yahnathu'
4
Understand the underlying principle
The oath's validity depends on the possibility of fulfillment. If the subject ceases to exist, fulfillment becomes impossible, so the oath is void from the start (or becomes void). Abu Yusuf considers the oath validly contracted and holds the swearer responsible for the impossibility.
The earlier 'jug issue' (mas'alat al-kuz) establishes that an oath on a non-existent subject is not contracted.
5
Apply to examples
For each example in the passage (killing Zayd, eating the loaf, paying the debt, informing about Amr, giving after permitter's death), identify whether the subject perishes and apply the ruling of the two.
The text consistently says 'la yahnathu 'indahuma' (he does not break it according to the two) for these cases.

وقد تفرع على هذا الأصل مسائل منها ما لو حلف ليقتلن زيداً اليوم فمات زيد قبل مضي اليوم لا يحنث عندهما كما سيأتي بيانه. ومنها لو حلف ليأكلن هذا الرغيف اليوم فأكله غيره قبل الليل. ومنها لو حلف ليقضين فلاناً دينه غداً وفلان قد مات ولا علم له أو مات أحدهما قبل مضي الغد أو قضاه قبله أو أبرأه فلان قبله لم تنعقد ومنها ما لو قال لزيد إن رأيت عمراً فلم أعلمك فعبدي حر فرآه مع زيد فسكت ولم يقل شيئاً أو قال هو عمر يعتق عندهما. ومنها لو حلف لا يعطيه حتى يأذن فلان فمات فلان ثم أعطاه لم يحنث، وكذا ولا ميتاً في آخر الوقت فالميت لا يوصف بالحنث . ولو هلك المحلوف عليه والوقت باق والحالف قائم بطلت اليمين عندهما وعند أبي يوسف يحنث . ا هـ باختصار قوله : (وأطلق المصنف الخ) قال الرملي : مقتضى ما اختاره في مسألة إن لم أقتل فلاناً من التفصيل بين العلم وعدمه أن يحمل إطلاقه هنا على عدم العلم حملاً للمطلق على المقيد ليكن ماشياً على وتيرة واحدة وإن كان في التبيين صحح رواية الإطلاق لاحتمال اختياره رواية التفصيل كالأسبيجابي فيكون في المسألة اختلاف التصحيح والترجيح كما هو ظاهر لكن الزيلعي فرق بين مسألة الكوز وبين مسألة القتل بأنه إذا كان عالماً فقد عقد يمينه على حياة يحدثها الله تعالى وهو متصور بخلاف مسألة الكوز فإن ما يحدثه الله تعالى فيه غير المحلوف عليه فيكون ما أطلقه هنا جارياً على إطلاقه تأمل ا هـ . أي لأن المحلوف عليه هنا ماء مظروف في الكوز وقت الحلف دون الحادث بعده قوله : (لم تنعقد) قال الرملي : عدم الانعقاد فيما إذا كان ميتاً وقت الحلف، أما إذا مات أحدهما قبل مضي الغد أو قضاه أو ابرأه قبله تبطل بعد الانعقاد إذ شرط بقاء المؤقتة إمكان البر وقد فات لكن ذكر في الجوهرة في شرح صعود السماء وقلب الحجر ذهباً أن المؤقتة يتعلق انعقادها بآخر الوقت عندهما . يعني ومحمداً فإذا كان كذلك فقوله «لم تنعقد صحيح في الكل، والذي يظهر من كلامهم أن في قولين : قيل بالبطلان بعد الانعقاد، وقيل بعدم الانعقاد إلا في آخر الوقت تأمل قوله: (ومنها لو حلف لا يعطيه حتى يأذن (فلان كذا في النسخ بدون تقييده باليوم وهو كذلك في الفتح. وانظر ما مسألة أبا حنيفة المسألة

كتاب الأيمان باب اليمين في الأكل والشرب واللبس والكلام ومنها ليضربنه أو ليكلمنه ومنها لو قال رجل لامرأته إن لم تهبي لي صداقك اليوم فأنت طالق وقال أبوها إن وهبت له صداقك فأمك طالق فحيلة عدم حنثهما أن تشتري منه بمهرها ثوباً ملفوفاً وتقبضه، فإذا مضى اليوم لم يحنث أبوها لأنها لم تهب صداقها ولا الزوج لأنها عجزت عن الهبة عند الغروب لأن الصداق سقط عن الزوج بالبيع، ثم إذا أرادت عود الصداق ردته بخيار الرؤية ; الكل في فتح القدير. ومنها ما في الولوالجية من تعليق الطلاق رجل قال إن لم أدخل الليلة البلد ولم ألق فلاناً فامرأته طالق فدخل ولم يصادفه في منزله فلم يلقه حتى أصبح إن كان عالماً بأنه غاب عن المنزل وقت الحلف يحنث، وإن لم يكن عالماً لا يحنث ا هـ . ما في المبتغى : وفي يمينه لامرأته إن لم تصل صلاة الفجر غداً فأنت كذا لا يحنث بحيضها بكرة في الأصح ا هـ. ومنها لو قال لامرأته بعد ما أصبح إن لم أجامعك هذه الليلة فأنت طالق ولم تكن له نية وكان يعلم أنه أصبح وقع يمينه على الليلة القابلة لأنه حلف نهاراً فينصرف إلى الليلة القابلة المستقبلة، وإن نوى تلك الليلة لا تنعقد اليمين عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد فرعاً لمسألة الكوز. ومنها قال إن نمت هذه الليلة في هذه الدار فامرأته كذا وقد انفجر الصبح وهو لا يعلم لا يحنث في يمينه لأن شرط الحنث وهو النوم في الليلة الماضية لا يتصور فصار كأنه قال إن صمت أمس فامرأته طالق لا يحنث في يمينه. ومنها ما لو قال إن لم أبت الليلة في هذه الدار والمسألة بحالها فكذلك في قولهما. ومنها لو غاب الرجل عن داره ساعة ثم رجع فظن أن المرأة غائبة عن الدار فقال إن لم آت بامرأتي إلى داري الليلة فهي طالق ثلاثاً فلما أصبح قالت المرأة كنت في هذه الدار لم يحنث عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن اليمين لم تنعقد، وإن قالت كنت غائبة، فإن صدقها الزوج طلقت لأن الزوج أقر بالطلاق. ومنها ما لو قال إن لم تردي الدينار الذي أخذتيه من كيسي فأنت طالق فإذا الدينار في كيسه

هذه الفرق بين وبين مسألة الكوز إذا أطلق وكان فيه ماء فصب قوله : (لأنها عجزت عن الهبة عند الغروب قال الرملي أي لم يمكنها ذلك إذ الهبة لا تتصور فيما سقط من المهر فالمراد من العجز هنا هو عدم الإمكان. وأقول : قد صرحوا بأن هبة الدين كالإبراء منه إلا في مسائل وأن الإبراء بعد قضاء الدين صحيح فمقتضاه صحة الهبة بعد ما ذكر إلا أن يفرق بين الهبة والبراءة في هذا فيكون مما استثنى هنا. وقد ذكر المصنف في الأشباه بعد قوله الإبراء بعد قضاء الدين صحيح وعن هذا لو علق طلاقها بإبرائها عن المهر ثم دفعه لها لا يبطل التعليق، فإذا أبرأته براءة إسقاط وقع ورجع عليها فتأمل هذا المحل ا هـ . وقد ذكر المؤلف مثل ذلك في باب التعليق في شرح قوله «وزوال الملك لا يبطل اليمين عند الكلام على المسألتين اللتين كثر وقوعهما فراجعه إن شئت قوله : (ومنها ما في الولوالجية الخ قال الرملي : التقييد بالعلم في هذه المسألة بناء على تقييد مسألة القتل والكوز به مسألة الرغيف وما شاكلها وهو قول الأسبيجابي، وقد صحح الزيلعي خلافه وعليه فلا يحنث لعدم إمكان تصور البر في آخر جزء من أجزاء الليلة مع غيبته عن المنزل قوله: (ومنها ما في المبتغى الخ) ا هـ. مطلقاً
And derived from this principle are issues: among them, if he swore to kill Zayd today and Zayd died before the day passed, he does not break his oath according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), as will come. Among them, if he swore to eat this loaf today and someone else ate it before night. Among them, if he swore to pay so-and-so his debt tomorrow and so-and-so had died and he has no knowledge, or one of them died before tomorrow passed, or he paid it before, or so-and-so released him before, the oath is not contracted. Among them, if he said to Zayd: 'If I see Amr and do not inform you, my slave is free,' and he saw him with Zayd and remained silent nor said anything, or said 'He is Amr,' it is effective (the slave is freed) according to the two. Among them, if he swore not to give him until so-and-so permits, and so-and-so died then he gave him, he does not break his oath. Likewise, no dead person at the end of time, for the dead is not described as breaking the oath. And if the subject of the oath perishes while the time remains and the swearer is alive, the oath is void according to the two, and according to Abu Yusuf he breaks it. End briefly. Qawluh (his statement): 'And the author gave an unqualified ruling...' Al-Ramli said... [the commentary continues similarly to lesson 1, repeating the same] ... Qawluh: 'It is not contracted' al-Ramli said: Non-contraction if he was dead at the time of the oath. But if one of them died before tomorrow passed, or he paid it or released him before, it becomes void after contraction, because the condition for the continuation of a temporal oath is the possibility of fulfillment, and it is lost. But in al-Jawhara, in the commentary on 'ascending the sky and turning stone into gold', it is mentioned that the contraction of a temporal oath is connected to the end of time according to the two, meaning Muhammad. If so, his statement 'not contracted' is correct in all cases. And what appears from their statements is that there are two sayings: some say it becomes void after contraction, some say it does not contract except at the last moment. Reflect. Qawluh: 'Among them, if he swore not to give him until so-and-so permits' [...] in the copies without restricting it to a day, and so it is in Fath al-Qadir. And consider the issue of Abu Hanifa. Then the chapter heading repeats, and then many more derived examples: including if he swore to beat him or speak to him; including if a man said to his wife: 'If you do not gift me your dower today, you are divorced,' and her father said: 'If she gifts you her dower, your mother is divorced,' then the trick to avoid both breaking their oaths is that she buys from him with her dower a wrapped garment and takes possession. When the day passes, her father does not break his oath because she did not gift her dower, and the husband does not break because she was unable to gift at sunset, as the dower has fallen from the husband due to the sale. Then if she wants the dower back, she returns it by option of inspection. All in Fath al-Qadir. And among them, what is in al-Walwaljiya regarding suspended divorce: a man said, 'If I do not enter the city tonight and do not meet so-and-so, my wife is divorced.' He entered but did not find him at his house, so he did not meet him until morning. If he knew that he was absent from the house at the time of the oath, he breaks his oath; if he did not know, he does not. End. What is in al-Mubtagha: In his oath to his wife, 'If you do not pray Fajr tomorrow, you are [divorced]' — she does not break her oath by menstruating in the morning according to the most correct. End. And among them, if he said to his wife after morning: 'If I do not have intercourse with you tonight, you are divorced,' and he had no intention and knew it was morning, his oath applies to the next night because he swore during the day, so it refers to the coming future night. And if he intended that night, the oath is not contracted according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as a branch of the jug issue. Among them, he said: 'If I sleep tonight in this house, my wife is [divorced],' and dawn broke without him knowing, he does not break his oath because the condition for breaking, i.e., sleeping in the past night, is not conceivable. It is as if he said: 'If I fasted yesterday, my wife is divorced,' he does not break his oath. Among them, if he said: 'If I do not spend the night in this house,' the issue being the same, likewise according to the two. Among them, if a man left his house for an hour then returned, and thought that his wife was absent from the house, so he said: 'If I do not bring my wife to my house tonight, she is thrice divorced.' When morning came, the wife said: 'I was in this house.' He does not break his oath according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because the oath was not contracted. And if she said: 'I was absent,' and the husband confirms her, she is divorced because the husband confessed to divorce. Among them, if he said: 'If you do not return the dinar that you took from my purse, you are divorced,' and the dinar is in his purse. This is the difference between the jug issue and this, if he gave an unqualified statement and there was water in it, he poured it. Qawluh: 'Because she was unable to gift at sunset' said al-Ramli: meaning she could not do that because a gift is inconceivable regarding what has fallen from the dower. So the meaning of inability here is the absence of possibility. And I say: They have explicitly stated that the gift of a debt is like acquittance from it except in some issues, and that acquittance after paying the debt is valid. So the implication is the validity of the gift after what was mentioned, unless there is a distinction between gift and acquittance in this matter, so it is among the exceptions. And the author mentioned in al-Ashbah after his statement 'acquittance after paying the debt is valid' that if he suspended her divorce on her acquitting him of the dower, then he pays it to her, the suspension is not invalidated. So if she acquits him with an acquittance of dropping, it occurs and he returns upon her. Reflect on this place. End. And the author mentioned similar in the chapter on suspension in his commentary on the statement 'And loss of ownership does not invalidate the oath' in the discussion on the two frequently occurring issues. So refer to it if you wish. Qawluh: 'Among them what is in al-Walwaljiya...' Al-Ramli said: The restriction to knowledge in this issue is based on the restriction of the killing issue and the jug issue, the loaf issue and similar ones, and it is the statement of al-Asbajabi. Al-Zayla'i authenticated the opposite, and accordingly he does not break his oath due to the impossibility of conceiving fulfillment in the last part of the night with his absence from the house. Qawluh: 'Among them what is in al-Mubtagha...' End. Absolutely.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lists numerous derivative rulings (masa'il) that branch from the general principle discussed earlier regarding oaths on subjects that may cease to exist or become impossible. The passage is an expansion probe on the earlier matn. The examples cover a wide range: oaths to kill someone who dies, to eat food that is eaten by another, to pay a debt to a deceased person, to inform of a sighting, to give something after a permitter dies, and many family-law related oaths involving divorce and dower. Key patterns include: the ruling often depends on whether the swearer knew of the impossibility at the time of the oath, following the distinction made by al-Asbajabi and others. In several cases, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ from Abu Yusuf alone (e.g., when the subject perishes while time remains: they say the oath is void, Abu Yusuf says he breaks it). The passage also presents a clever legal trick (hila) in the dower case: the wife buys a garment from her husband using her dower as payment, thus making the dower cease to exist as a debt, so that the husband's oath (if she does not gift) is not broken because she is no longer able to gift what is no longer owed, and the father's oath (if she does gift) is also not broken because she did not actually gift. The commentary by al-Ramli clarifies nuances about gift of a debt versus acquittance. The overall coherence is maintained by referring back to the original jug issue and the killing issue.

Key Terms
يمين مؤقتة (yamin muwaqqata): A temporal oath, i.e., an oath restricted to a specific time period, such as 'today' or 'tonight'.
حنث (hanth): Breaking an oath; violating the condition sworn upon, triggering kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a man who swore to kill Zayd today, and Zayd died before the day ended, what is the ruling according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)?
A) The man breaks his oath and must pay kaffarah.
B) The oath is void and he does not break it.
C) He breaks his oath only if he knew of Zayd's death.
D) The oath remains valid until the end of the day.

Key Takeaway
When the subject of a temporal oath perishes before the deadline, the oath is void (batil) according to the majority (the two), not broken (hanth), so no kaffarah is due.

10 min
Legal Stratagem (Hila) to Avoid Breaking Oaths on Dower
Legal stratagem (hila) to avoid breaking oaths in a dower-related conditional divorce scenario

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi legal stratagem (hila) used when a husband and father-in-law both conditionally swear divorce regarding the wife's dower, and explain why it works.

Core Idea
A clever purchase using the dower can prevent both oaths from being broken when husband and father-in-law both swear conditional divorce on the same dower gift.

Sometimes a husband and his father-in-law both make conditional oaths involving the wife's dower, creating a deadlock where both would break their oaths. The Hanafi jurists devised a legal stratagem (hila) using a sale and option of inspection to avoid both oaths being violated. This lesson unpacks that stratagem and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
The husband swears: 'If you do not gift me your dower today, you are divorced.' The father swears: 'If she gifts you her dower, your mother is divorced.' If she gifts, she causes her mother's divorce; if she doesn't, she causes her own divorce.
This creates a situation where any action leads to a divorce.
2
Introduce the hila
The trick is that the wife buys a wrapped garment (thawban malfufan) from her husband using her dower as payment. She takes possession of the garment.
The dower is now transformed into the price of the garment; it is no longer owed as a dower.
3
Analyze the effect on the husband's oath
The husband's oath was conditional on her gifting the dower. Since the dower is no longer owed (it has been used to pay for the garment), she is unable to gift it at sunset. Therefore, she does not break her oath by failing to gift—she is physically unable.
Inability (ghayr mumkin) prevents the condition from being fulfilled.
4
Analyze the effect on the father's oath
The father's oath was conditional on her gifting the dower. Since she did not actually gift it (she used it in a sale), she has not performed the act that would trigger his oath.
The father's oath condition 'if she gifts' was not activated.
5
Consider the return of the garment
After the day passes and both oaths are avoided, the wife can return the garment using the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'ya) to reclaim her dower, restoring the original situation.
This completes the stratagem without sin.

Source Text

وقد تفرع على هذا الأصل مسائل منها ما لو حلف ليقتلن زيداً اليوم فمات زيد قبل مضي اليوم لا يحنث عندهما كما سيأتي بيانه. ومنها لو حلف ليأكلن هذا الرغيف اليوم فأكله غيره قبل الليل. ومنها لو حلف ليقضين فلاناً دينه غداً وفلان قد مات ولا علم له أو مات أحدهما قبل مضي الغد أو قضاه قبله أو أبرأه فلان قبله لم تنعقد ومنها ما لو قال لزيد إن رأيت عمراً فلم أعلمك فعبدي حر فرآه مع زيد فسكت ولم يقل شيئاً أو قال هو عمر يعتق عندهما. ومنها لو حلف لا يعطيه حتى يأذن فلان فمات فلان ثم أعطاه لم يحنث، وكذا ولا ميتاً في آخر الوقت فالميت لا يوصف بالحنث . ولو هلك المحلوف عليه والوقت باق والحالف قائم بطلت اليمين عندهما وعند أبي يوسف يحنث . ا هـ باختصار قوله : (وأطلق المصنف الخ) قال الرملي : مقتضى ما اختاره في مسألة إن لم أقتل فلاناً من التفصيل بين العلم وعدمه أن يحمل إطلاقه هنا على عدم العلم حملاً للمطلق على المقيد ليكن ماشياً على وتيرة واحدة وإن كان في التبيين صحح رواية الإطلاق لاحتمال اختياره رواية التفصيل كالأسبيجابي فيكون في المسألة اختلاف التصحيح والترجيح كما هو ظاهر لكن الزيلعي فرق بين مسألة الكوز وبين مسألة القتل بأنه إذا كان عالماً فقد عقد يمينه على حياة يحدثها الله تعالى وهو متصور بخلاف مسألة الكوز فإن ما يحدثه الله تعالى فيه غير المحلوف عليه فيكون ما أطلقه هنا جارياً على إطلاقه تأمل ا هـ . أي لأن المحلوف عليه هنا ماء مظروف في الكوز وقت الحلف دون الحادث بعده قوله : (لم تنعقد) قال الرملي : عدم الانعقاد فيما إذا كان ميتاً وقت الحلف، أما إذا مات أحدهما قبل مضي الغد أو قضاه أو ابرأه قبله تبطل بعد الانعقاد إذ شرط بقاء المؤقتة إمكان البر وقد فات لكن ذكر في الجوهرة في شرح صعود السماء وقلب الحجر ذهباً أن المؤقتة يتعلق انعقادها بآخر الوقت عندهما . يعني ومحمداً فإذا كان كذلك فقوله «لم تنعقد صحيح في الكل، والذي يظهر من كلامهم أن في قولين : قيل بالبطلان بعد الانعقاد، وقيل بعدم الانعقاد إلا في آخر الوقت تأمل قوله: (ومنها لو حلف لا يعطيه حتى يأذن (فلان كذا في النسخ بدون تقييده باليوم وهو كذلك في الفتح. وانظر ما مسألة أبا حنيفة المسألة

كتاب الأيمان باب اليمين في الأكل والشرب واللبس والكلام ومنها ليضربنه أو ليكلمنه ومنها لو قال رجل لامرأته إن لم تهبي لي صداقك اليوم فأنت طالق وقال أبوها إن وهبت له صداقك فأمك طالق فحيلة عدم حنثهما أن تشتري منه بمهرها ثوباً ملفوفاً وتقبضه، فإذا مضى اليوم لم يحنث أبوها لأنها لم تهب صداقها ولا الزوج لأنها عجزت عن الهبة عند الغروب لأن الصداق سقط عن الزوج بالبيع، ثم إذا أرادت عود الصداق ردته بخيار الرؤية ; الكل في فتح القدير. ومنها ما في الولوالجية من تعليق الطلاق رجل قال إن لم أدخل الليلة البلد ولم ألق فلاناً فامرأته طالق فدخل ولم يصادفه في منزله فلم يلقه حتى أصبح إن كان عالماً بأنه غاب عن المنزل وقت الحلف يحنث، وإن لم يكن عالماً لا يحنث ا هـ . ما في المبتغى : وفي يمينه لامرأته إن لم تصل صلاة الفجر غداً فأنت كذا لا يحنث بحيضها بكرة في الأصح ا هـ. ومنها لو قال لامرأته بعد ما أصبح إن لم أجامعك هذه الليلة فأنت طالق ولم تكن له نية وكان يعلم أنه أصبح وقع يمينه على الليلة القابلة لأنه حلف نهاراً فينصرف إلى الليلة القابلة المستقبلة، وإن نوى تلك الليلة لا تنعقد اليمين عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد فرعاً لمسألة الكوز. ومنها قال إن نمت هذه الليلة في هذه الدار فامرأته كذا وقد انفجر الصبح وهو لا يعلم لا يحنث في يمينه لأن شرط الحنث وهو النوم في الليلة الماضية لا يتصور فصار كأنه قال إن صمت أمس فامرأته طالق لا يحنث في يمينه. ومنها ما لو قال إن لم أبت الليلة في هذه الدار والمسألة بحالها فكذلك في قولهما. ومنها لو غاب الرجل عن داره ساعة ثم رجع فظن أن المرأة غائبة عن الدار فقال إن لم آت بامرأتي إلى داري الليلة فهي طالق ثلاثاً فلما أصبح قالت المرأة كنت في هذه الدار لم يحنث عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن اليمين لم تنعقد، وإن قالت كنت غائبة، فإن صدقها الزوج طلقت لأن الزوج أقر بالطلاق. ومنها ما لو قال إن لم تردي الدينار الذي أخذتيه من كيسي فأنت طالق فإذا الدينار في كيسه

هذه الفرق بين وبين مسألة الكوز إذا أطلق وكان فيه ماء فصب قوله : (لأنها عجزت عن الهبة عند الغروب قال الرملي أي لم يمكنها ذلك إذ الهبة لا تتصور فيما سقط من المهر فالمراد من العجز هنا هو عدم الإمكان. وأقول : قد صرحوا بأن هبة الدين كالإبراء منه إلا في مسائل وأن الإبراء بعد قضاء الدين صحيح فمقتضاه صحة الهبة بعد ما ذكر إلا أن يفرق بين الهبة والبراءة في هذا فيكون مما استثنى هنا. وقد ذكر المصنف في الأشباه بعد قوله الإبراء بعد قضاء الدين صحيح وعن هذا لو علق طلاقها بإبرائها عن المهر ثم دفعه لها لا يبطل التعليق، فإذا أبرأته براءة إسقاط وقع ورجع عليها فتأمل هذا المحل ا هـ . وقد ذكر المؤلف مثل ذلك في باب التعليق في شرح قوله «وزوال الملك لا يبطل اليمين عند الكلام على المسألتين اللتين كثر وقوعهما فراجعه إن شئت قوله : (ومنها ما في الولوالجية الخ قال الرملي : التقييد بالعلم في هذه المسألة بناء على تقييد مسألة القتل والكوز به مسألة الرغيف وما شاكلها وهو قول الأسبيجابي، وقد صحح الزيلعي خلافه وعليه فلا يحنث لعدم إمكان تصور البر في آخر جزء من أجزاء الليلة مع غيبته عن المنزل قوله: (ومنها ما في المبتغى الخ) ا هـ. مطلقاً
And derived from this principle are issues: among them, if he swore to kill Zayd today and Zayd died before the day passed, he does not break his oath according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), as will come. Among them, if he swore to eat this loaf today and someone else ate it before night. Among them, if he swore to pay so-and-so his debt tomorrow and so-and-so had died and he has no knowledge, or one of them died before tomorrow passed, or he paid it before, or so-and-so released him before, the oath is not contracted. Among them, if he said to Zayd: 'If I see Amr and do not inform you, my slave is free,' and he saw him with Zayd and remained silent nor said anything, or said 'He is Amr,' it is effective (the slave is freed) according to the two. Among them, if he swore not to give him until so-and-so permits, and so-and-so died then he gave him, he does not break his oath. Likewise, no dead person at the end of time, for the dead is not described as breaking the oath. And if the subject of the oath perishes while the time remains and the swearer is alive, the oath is void according to the two, and according to Abu Yusuf he breaks it. End briefly. Qawluh (his statement): 'And the author gave an unqualified ruling...' Al-Ramli said... [the commentary continues similarly to lesson 1, repeating the same] ... Qawluh: 'It is not contracted' al-Ramli said: Non-contraction if he was dead at the time of the oath. But if one of them died before tomorrow passed, or he paid it or released him before, it becomes void after contraction, because the condition for the continuation of a temporal oath is the possibility of fulfillment, and it is lost. But in al-Jawhara, in the commentary on 'ascending the sky and turning stone into gold', it is mentioned that the contraction of a temporal oath is connected to the end of time according to the two, meaning Muhammad. If so, his statement 'not contracted' is correct in all cases. And what appears from their statements is that there are two sayings: some say it becomes void after contraction, some say it does not contract except at the last moment. Reflect. Qawluh: 'Among them, if he swore not to give him until so-and-so permits' [...] in the copies without restricting it to a day, and so it is in Fath al-Qadir. And consider the issue of Abu Hanifa. Then the chapter heading repeats, and then many more derived examples: including if he swore to beat him or speak to him; including if a man said to his wife: 'If you do not gift me your dower today, you are divorced,' and her father said: 'If she gifts you her dower, your mother is divorced,' then the trick to avoid both breaking their oaths is that she buys from him with her dower a wrapped garment and takes possession. When the day passes, her father does not break his oath because she did not gift her dower, and the husband does not break because she was unable to gift at sunset, as the dower has fallen from the husband due to the sale. Then if she wants the dower back, she returns it by option of inspection. All in Fath al-Qadir. And among them, what is in al-Walwaljiya regarding suspended divorce: a man said, 'If I do not enter the city tonight and do not meet so-and-so, my wife is divorced.' He entered but did not find him at his house, so he did not meet him until morning. If he knew that he was absent from the house at the time of the oath, he breaks his oath; if he did not know, he does not. End. What is in al-Mubtagha: In his oath to his wife, 'If you do not pray Fajr tomorrow, you are [divorced]' — she does not break her oath by menstruating in the morning according to the most correct. End. And among them, if he said to his wife after morning: 'If I do not have intercourse with you tonight, you are divorced,' and he had no intention and knew it was morning, his oath applies to the next night because he swore during the day, so it refers to the coming future night. And if he intended that night, the oath is not contracted according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as a branch of the jug issue. Among them, he said: 'If I sleep tonight in this house, my wife is [divorced],' and dawn broke without him knowing, he does not break his oath because the condition for breaking, i.e., sleeping in the past night, is not conceivable. It is as if he said: 'If I fasted yesterday, my wife is divorced,' he does not break his oath. Among them, if he said: 'If I do not spend the night in this house,' the issue being the same, likewise according to the two. Among them, if a man left his house for an hour then returned, and thought that his wife was absent from the house, so he said: 'If I do not bring my wife to my house tonight, she is thrice divorced.' When morning came, the wife said: 'I was in this house.' He does not break his oath according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because the oath was not contracted. And if she said: 'I was absent,' and the husband confirms her, she is divorced because the husband confessed to divorce. Among them, if he said: 'If you do not return the dinar that you took from my purse, you are divorced,' and the dinar is in his purse. This is the difference between the jug issue and this, if he gave an unqualified statement and there was water in it, he poured it. Qawluh: 'Because she was unable to gift at sunset' said al-Ramli: meaning she could not do that because a gift is inconceivable regarding what has fallen from the dower. So the meaning of inability here is the absence of possibility. And I say: They have explicitly stated that the gift of a debt is like acquittance from it except in some issues, and that acquittance after paying the debt is valid. So the implication is the validity of the gift after what was mentioned, unless there is a distinction between gift and acquittance in this matter, so it is among the exceptions. And the author mentioned in al-Ashbah after his statement 'acquittance after paying the debt is valid' that if he suspended her divorce on her acquitting him of the dower, then he pays it to her, the suspension is not invalidated. So if she acquits him with an acquittance of dropping, it occurs and he returns upon her. Reflect on this place. End. And the author mentioned similar in the chapter on suspension in his commentary on the statement 'And loss of ownership does not invalidate the oath' in the discussion on the two frequently occurring issues. So refer to it if you wish. Qawluh: 'Among them what is in al-Walwaljiya...' Al-Ramli said: The restriction to knowledge in this issue is based on the restriction of the killing issue and the jug issue, the loaf issue and similar ones, and it is the statement of al-Asbajabi. Al-Zayla'i authenticated the opposite, and accordingly he does not break his oath due to the impossibility of conceiving fulfillment in the last part of the night with his absence from the house. Qawluh: 'Among them what is in al-Mubtagha...' End. Absolutely.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lists numerous derivative rulings (masa'il) that branch from the general principle discussed earlier regarding oaths on subjects that may cease to exist or become impossible. The passage is an expansion probe on the earlier matn. The examples cover a wide range: oaths to kill someone who dies, to eat food that is eaten by another, to pay a debt to a deceased person, to inform of a sighting, to give something after a permitter dies, and many family-law related oaths involving divorce and dower. Key patterns include: the ruling often depends on whether the swearer knew of the impossibility at the time of the oath, following the distinction made by al-Asbajabi and others. In several cases, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ from Abu Yusuf alone (e.g., when the subject perishes while time remains: they say the oath is void, Abu Yusuf says he breaks it). The passage also presents a clever legal trick (hila) in the dower case: the wife buys a garment from her husband using her dower as payment, thus making the dower cease to exist as a debt, so that the husband's oath (if she does not gift) is not broken because she is no longer able to gift what is no longer owed, and the father's oath (if she does gift) is also not broken because she did not actually gift. The commentary by al-Ramli clarifies nuances about gift of a debt versus acquittance. The overall coherence is maintained by referring back to the original jug issue and the killing issue.

Key Terms
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem or trick to avoid violating an oath or to achieve a permissible outcome without sin.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): Option of inspection: the right to return a purchased item if it was not seen before the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the husband not break his oath in the dower hila scenario?
A) Because he forgot about his oath.
B) Because the wife technically did not gift the dower; she used it to buy a garment.
C) Because the father's oath overrides the husband's.
D) Because the wife returned the dower before sunset.

Key Takeaway
When conflicting oaths on the same dower create a deadlock, a genuine sale of a garment using the dower as price, followed by return via option of inspection, is a permissible stratagem to avoid breaking both oaths.

9 min
Role of Knowledge in Temporal Oaths and Suspended Divorce
Derived rulings on oaths and suspended divorce where knowledge of impossibility is at issue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze how the swearer's knowledge (or ignorance) of the impossibility of fulfillment affects the ruling of a temporal oath, particularly in ta'liq al-talaq cases.

Core Idea
If the swearer was unaware of the impossibility at the time of the oath, the oath is not contracted; if aware, it is contracted then becomes void.

Temporal oaths on impossible subjects raise the question: did the swearer know of the impossibility? The Hanafi school has a disputed view on this. Al-Asbajabi holds that knowledge is essential for the oath to be contracted; al-Zayla'i rejects that restriction. This lesson examines cases like entering a city when the person is absent, and sleeping when dawn has already broken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of knowledge
In the Walwaljiya case, a man swears: 'If I do not enter the city tonight and do not meet so-and-so, my wife is divorced.' He enters but does not meet him because the man was absent. The ruling depends on whether the swearer knew at the time of the oath that the man was absent.
Knowledge of the absence affects whether the oath is contracted.
2
Understand the two positions
Al-Asbajabi restricts the general principle by requiring that the swearer knew the impossibility. Al-Zayla'i rejects this, saying the oath is void regardless of knowledge.
The text says: 'al-Zayla'i authenticated the opposite.'
3
Apply to the sleeping case
A man swears not to sleep tonight in his house, but dawn breaks without him knowing. The condition 'sleep tonight' is now impossible because the night has passed. If he knew it was dawn, the oath would be void; if he did not know, al-Asbajabi says no oath, al-Zayla'i says still void.
The principle parallels the jug issue.
4
Apply to the menstruation case
A man swears that if his wife does not pray Fajr tomorrow, she is divorced. She menstruates in the morning, making prayer impossible. The ruling: she does not break her oath according to the most correct view.
Menstruation prevents the prayer, so the oath is void due to impossibility.
5
Apply to the case of the dinar
A man swears: 'If you do not return the dinar you took from my purse, you are divorced.' The dinar is found in his purse. The oath is void because the subject (the dinar) was always possible to return; the condition is impossible to fulfill (she cannot return what is already there).
This distinguishes from the jug issue where water was poured and replenished.

وقد تفرع على هذا الأصل مسائل منها ما لو حلف ليقتلن زيداً اليوم فمات زيد قبل مضي اليوم لا يحنث عندهما كما سيأتي بيانه. ومنها لو حلف ليأكلن هذا الرغيف اليوم فأكله غيره قبل الليل. ومنها لو حلف ليقضين فلاناً دينه غداً وفلان قد مات ولا علم له أو مات أحدهما قبل مضي الغد أو قضاه قبله أو أبرأه فلان قبله لم تنعقد ومنها ما لو قال لزيد إن رأيت عمراً فلم أعلمك فعبدي حر فرآه مع زيد فسكت ولم يقل شيئاً أو قال هو عمر يعتق عندهما. ومنها لو حلف لا يعطيه حتى يأذن فلان فمات فلان ثم أعطاه لم يحنث، وكذا ولا ميتاً في آخر الوقت فالميت لا يوصف بالحنث . ولو هلك المحلوف عليه والوقت باق والحالف قائم بطلت اليمين عندهما وعند أبي يوسف يحنث . ا هـ باختصار قوله : (وأطلق المصنف الخ) قال الرملي : مقتضى ما اختاره في مسألة إن لم أقتل فلاناً من التفصيل بين العلم وعدمه أن يحمل إطلاقه هنا على عدم العلم حملاً للمطلق على المقيد ليكن ماشياً على وتيرة واحدة وإن كان في التبيين صحح رواية الإطلاق لاحتمال اختياره رواية التفصيل كالأسبيجابي فيكون في المسألة اختلاف التصحيح والترجيح كما هو ظاهر لكن الزيلعي فرق بين مسألة الكوز وبين مسألة القتل بأنه إذا كان عالماً فقد عقد يمينه على حياة يحدثها الله تعالى وهو متصور بخلاف مسألة الكوز فإن ما يحدثه الله تعالى فيه غير المحلوف عليه فيكون ما أطلقه هنا جارياً على إطلاقه تأمل ا هـ . أي لأن المحلوف عليه هنا ماء مظروف في الكوز وقت الحلف دون الحادث بعده قوله : (لم تنعقد) قال الرملي : عدم الانعقاد فيما إذا كان ميتاً وقت الحلف، أما إذا مات أحدهما قبل مضي الغد أو قضاه أو ابرأه قبله تبطل بعد الانعقاد إذ شرط بقاء المؤقتة إمكان البر وقد فات لكن ذكر في الجوهرة في شرح صعود السماء وقلب الحجر ذهباً أن المؤقتة يتعلق انعقادها بآخر الوقت عندهما . يعني ومحمداً فإذا كان كذلك فقوله «لم تنعقد صحيح في الكل، والذي يظهر من كلامهم أن في قولين : قيل بالبطلان بعد الانعقاد، وقيل بعدم الانعقاد إلا في آخر الوقت تأمل قوله: (ومنها لو حلف لا يعطيه حتى يأذن (فلان كذا في النسخ بدون تقييده باليوم وهو كذلك في الفتح. وانظر ما مسألة أبا حنيفة المسألة

كتاب الأيمان باب اليمين في الأكل والشرب واللبس والكلام ومنها ليضربنه أو ليكلمنه ومنها لو قال رجل لامرأته إن لم تهبي لي صداقك اليوم فأنت طالق وقال أبوها إن وهبت له صداقك فأمك طالق فحيلة عدم حنثهما أن تشتري منه بمهرها ثوباً ملفوفاً وتقبضه، فإذا مضى اليوم لم يحنث أبوها لأنها لم تهب صداقها ولا الزوج لأنها عجزت عن الهبة عند الغروب لأن الصداق سقط عن الزوج بالبيع، ثم إذا أرادت عود الصداق ردته بخيار الرؤية ; الكل في فتح القدير. ومنها ما في الولوالجية من تعليق الطلاق رجل قال إن لم أدخل الليلة البلد ولم ألق فلاناً فامرأته طالق فدخل ولم يصادفه في منزله فلم يلقه حتى أصبح إن كان عالماً بأنه غاب عن المنزل وقت الحلف يحنث، وإن لم يكن عالماً لا يحنث ا هـ . ما في المبتغى : وفي يمينه لامرأته إن لم تصل صلاة الفجر غداً فأنت كذا لا يحنث بحيضها بكرة في الأصح ا هـ. ومنها لو قال لامرأته بعد ما أصبح إن لم أجامعك هذه الليلة فأنت طالق ولم تكن له نية وكان يعلم أنه أصبح وقع يمينه على الليلة القابلة لأنه حلف نهاراً فينصرف إلى الليلة القابلة المستقبلة، وإن نوى تلك الليلة لا تنعقد اليمين عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد فرعاً لمسألة الكوز. ومنها قال إن نمت هذه الليلة في هذه الدار فامرأته كذا وقد انفجر الصبح وهو لا يعلم لا يحنث في يمينه لأن شرط الحنث وهو النوم في الليلة الماضية لا يتصور فصار كأنه قال إن صمت أمس فامرأته طالق لا يحنث في يمينه. ومنها ما لو قال إن لم أبت الليلة في هذه الدار والمسألة بحالها فكذلك في قولهما. ومنها لو غاب الرجل عن داره ساعة ثم رجع فظن أن المرأة غائبة عن الدار فقال إن لم آت بامرأتي إلى داري الليلة فهي طالق ثلاثاً فلما أصبح قالت المرأة كنت في هذه الدار لم يحنث عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن اليمين لم تنعقد، وإن قالت كنت غائبة، فإن صدقها الزوج طلقت لأن الزوج أقر بالطلاق. ومنها ما لو قال إن لم تردي الدينار الذي أخذتيه من كيسي فأنت طالق فإذا الدينار في كيسه

هذه الفرق بين وبين مسألة الكوز إذا أطلق وكان فيه ماء فصب قوله : (لأنها عجزت عن الهبة عند الغروب قال الرملي أي لم يمكنها ذلك إذ الهبة لا تتصور فيما سقط من المهر فالمراد من العجز هنا هو عدم الإمكان. وأقول : قد صرحوا بأن هبة الدين كالإبراء منه إلا في مسائل وأن الإبراء بعد قضاء الدين صحيح فمقتضاه صحة الهبة بعد ما ذكر إلا أن يفرق بين الهبة والبراءة في هذا فيكون مما استثنى هنا. وقد ذكر المصنف في الأشباه بعد قوله الإبراء بعد قضاء الدين صحيح وعن هذا لو علق طلاقها بإبرائها عن المهر ثم دفعه لها لا يبطل التعليق، فإذا أبرأته براءة إسقاط وقع ورجع عليها فتأمل هذا المحل ا هـ . وقد ذكر المؤلف مثل ذلك في باب التعليق في شرح قوله «وزوال الملك لا يبطل اليمين عند الكلام على المسألتين اللتين كثر وقوعهما فراجعه إن شئت قوله : (ومنها ما في الولوالجية الخ قال الرملي : التقييد بالعلم في هذه المسألة بناء على تقييد مسألة القتل والكوز به مسألة الرغيف وما شاكلها وهو قول الأسبيجابي، وقد صحح الزيلعي خلافه وعليه فلا يحنث لعدم إمكان تصور البر في آخر جزء من أجزاء الليلة مع غيبته عن المنزل قوله: (ومنها ما في المبتغى الخ) ا هـ. مطلقاً
And derived from this principle are issues: among them, if he swore to kill Zayd today and Zayd died before the day passed, he does not break his oath according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), as will come. Among them, if he swore to eat this loaf today and someone else ate it before night. Among them, if he swore to pay so-and-so his debt tomorrow and so-and-so had died and he has no knowledge, or one of them died before tomorrow passed, or he paid it before, or so-and-so released him before, the oath is not contracted. Among them, if he said to Zayd: 'If I see Amr and do not inform you, my slave is free,' and he saw him with Zayd and remained silent nor said anything, or said 'He is Amr,' it is effective (the slave is freed) according to the two. Among them, if he swore not to give him until so-and-so permits, and so-and-so died then he gave him, he does not break his oath. Likewise, no dead person at the end of time, for the dead is not described as breaking the oath. And if the subject of the oath perishes while the time remains and the swearer is alive, the oath is void according to the two, and according to Abu Yusuf he breaks it. End briefly. Qawluh (his statement): 'And the author gave an unqualified ruling...' Al-Ramli said... [the commentary continues similarly to lesson 1, repeating the same] ... Qawluh: 'It is not contracted' al-Ramli said: Non-contraction if he was dead at the time of the oath. But if one of them died before tomorrow passed, or he paid it or released him before, it becomes void after contraction, because the condition for the continuation of a temporal oath is the possibility of fulfillment, and it is lost. But in al-Jawhara, in the commentary on 'ascending the sky and turning stone into gold', it is mentioned that the contraction of a temporal oath is connected to the end of time according to the two, meaning Muhammad. If so, his statement 'not contracted' is correct in all cases. And what appears from their statements is that there are two sayings: some say it becomes void after contraction, some say it does not contract except at the last moment. Reflect. Qawluh: 'Among them, if he swore not to give him until so-and-so permits' [...] in the copies without restricting it to a day, and so it is in Fath al-Qadir. And consider the issue of Abu Hanifa. Then the chapter heading repeats, and then many more derived examples: including if he swore to beat him or speak to him; including if a man said to his wife: 'If you do not gift me your dower today, you are divorced,' and her father said: 'If she gifts you her dower, your mother is divorced,' then the trick to avoid both breaking their oaths is that she buys from him with her dower a wrapped garment and takes possession. When the day passes, her father does not break his oath because she did not gift her dower, and the husband does not break because she was unable to gift at sunset, as the dower has fallen from the husband due to the sale. Then if she wants the dower back, she returns it by option of inspection. All in Fath al-Qadir. And among them, what is in al-Walwaljiya regarding suspended divorce: a man said, 'If I do not enter the city tonight and do not meet so-and-so, my wife is divorced.' He entered but did not find him at his house, so he did not meet him until morning. If he knew that he was absent from the house at the time of the oath, he breaks his oath; if he did not know, he does not. End. What is in al-Mubtagha: In his oath to his wife, 'If you do not pray Fajr tomorrow, you are [divorced]' — she does not break her oath by menstruating in the morning according to the most correct. End. And among them, if he said to his wife after morning: 'If I do not have intercourse with you tonight, you are divorced,' and he had no intention and knew it was morning, his oath applies to the next night because he swore during the day, so it refers to the coming future night. And if he intended that night, the oath is not contracted according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as a branch of the jug issue. Among them, he said: 'If I sleep tonight in this house, my wife is [divorced],' and dawn broke without him knowing, he does not break his oath because the condition for breaking, i.e., sleeping in the past night, is not conceivable. It is as if he said: 'If I fasted yesterday, my wife is divorced,' he does not break his oath. Among them, if he said: 'If I do not spend the night in this house,' the issue being the same, likewise according to the two. Among them, if a man left his house for an hour then returned, and thought that his wife was absent from the house, so he said: 'If I do not bring my wife to my house tonight, she is thrice divorced.' When morning came, the wife said: 'I was in this house.' He does not break his oath according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because the oath was not contracted. And if she said: 'I was absent,' and the husband confirms her, she is divorced because the husband confessed to divorce. Among them, if he said: 'If you do not return the dinar that you took from my purse, you are divorced,' and the dinar is in his purse. This is the difference between the jug issue and this, if he gave an unqualified statement and there was water in it, he poured it. Qawluh: 'Because she was unable to gift at sunset' said al-Ramli: meaning she could not do that because a gift is inconceivable regarding what has fallen from the dower. So the meaning of inability here is the absence of possibility. And I say: They have explicitly stated that the gift of a debt is like acquittance from it except in some issues, and that acquittance after paying the debt is valid. So the implication is the validity of the gift after what was mentioned, unless there is a distinction between gift and acquittance in this matter, so it is among the exceptions. And the author mentioned in al-Ashbah after his statement 'acquittance after paying the debt is valid' that if he suspended her divorce on her acquitting him of the dower, then he pays it to her, the suspension is not invalidated. So if she acquits him with an acquittance of dropping, it occurs and he returns upon her. Reflect on this place. End. And the author mentioned similar in the chapter on suspension in his commentary on the statement 'And loss of ownership does not invalidate the oath' in the discussion on the two frequently occurring issues. So refer to it if you wish. Qawluh: 'Among them what is in al-Walwaljiya...' Al-Ramli said: The restriction to knowledge in this issue is based on the restriction of the killing issue and the jug issue, the loaf issue and similar ones, and it is the statement of al-Asbajabi. Al-Zayla'i authenticated the opposite, and accordingly he does not break his oath due to the impossibility of conceiving fulfillment in the last part of the night with his absence from the house. Qawluh: 'Among them what is in al-Mubtagha...' End. Absolutely.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lists numerous derivative rulings (masa'il) that branch from the general principle discussed earlier regarding oaths on subjects that may cease to exist or become impossible. The passage is an expansion probe on the earlier matn. The examples cover a wide range: oaths to kill someone who dies, to eat food that is eaten by another, to pay a debt to a deceased person, to inform of a sighting, to give something after a permitter dies, and many family-law related oaths involving divorce and dower. Key patterns include: the ruling often depends on whether the swearer knew of the impossibility at the time of the oath, following the distinction made by al-Asbajabi and others. In several cases, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ from Abu Yusuf alone (e.g., when the subject perishes while time remains: they say the oath is void, Abu Yusuf says he breaks it). The passage also presents a clever legal trick (hila) in the dower case: the wife buys a garment from her husband using her dower as payment, thus making the dower cease to exist as a debt, so that the husband's oath (if she does not gift) is not broken because she is no longer able to gift what is no longer owed, and the father's oath (if she does gift) is also not broken because she did not actually gift. The commentary by al-Ramli clarifies nuances about gift of a debt versus acquittance. The overall coherence is maintained by referring back to the original jug issue and the killing issue.

Key Terms
تعليق الطلاق (ta'liq al-talaq): Suspending divorce on a condition; if the condition occurs, the divorce takes effect.
علم ('ilm): Knowledge; here it refers to the swearer's awareness of the impossibility at the time of the oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Asbajabi, if a man swears to meet someone tonight not knowing that person is out of town, what is the ruling?
A) The oath is void; no hanth.
B) The oath is not contracted; no hanth.
C) The oath is contracted and broken; kaffarah required.
D) The oath is suspended until he gains knowledge.

Key Takeaway
In temporal oaths on impossible subjects, the Hanafi school is divided on whether the swearer's knowledge matters; the preferred view (al-Zayla'i) holds the oath void regardless.

Swearing to Do the Impossible: Hanafi Ruling vs Zufar
Ruling on oaths for impossible acts with Hanafi response to Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on oaths for customarily impossible acts and distinguish it from Zufar's position.

Core Idea
An oath for a customarily impossible act is valid because divine power makes it possible; the oath is broken immediately.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common question: if someone swears to do something impossible by custom, like climbing the sky, is the oath valid? The Hanafi school, responding to Zufar, distinguishes between real impossibility and customary impossibility, leading to a clear ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
The matn states: if someone swears to ascend the sky or turn a stone into gold, he breaks the oath immediately (حنث للحال). Note that this is the Hanafi position.
The act is impossible by custom but possible in reality.
2
Zufar's objection
Zufar argues the oath is not contracted because the act is impossible by custom, resembling real impossibility.
He analogizes customary impossibility to real impossibility.
3
Hanafi proof (dalil)
The Hanafi response: fulfillment is conceivable in reality. Angels ascend the sky, and Allah can transform matter. Therefore the oath is contracted.
The key is that real possibility, even if impossible by custom, suffices for contract.
4
Application of the rule: analogy to death
If a dying person swears and dies, the oath is broken despite the theoretical possibility of revival. Similarly, here the oath is broken due to customary incapacity.
Customary incapacity triggers immediate breaking, not non-contract.
5
Distinguishing counterexample: the jug
If someone swears to drink water from a jug that has no water at the time of swearing, the oath is not contracted because fulfillment is inconceivable even in reality.
Real impossibility prevents contract; customary impossibility does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (حلف ليصعدن السماء أو ليقلبن هذا الحجر ذهباً حنث للحال) وقال زفر : لا تنعقد لأنه مستحيل عادة فأشبه المستحيل حقيقة ولنا أن البر متصور حقيقة - بكسر الواو - أي ممكن لأن الصعود إلى السماء ممكن حقيقة ألا ترى أن الملائكة يصعدونها، وكذا تحول الحجر ذهباً بتحويل الله تعالى بجعله صفة الحجرية صفة الذهبية أو بإعدام الأجراء الحجرية وإبدالها بأجزاء ذهبية، فالتحويل في الأول أظهر وهو ممكن عند المتكلمين على ما هو الحق، وإذا كان متصوراً تنعقد اليمين موجبة لحلفة ثم يحنث بحكم العجز الثابث عادة كما إذا مات الحالف فإنه يحنث مع احتمال إعادة الحياة، وبخلاف مسألة الكوز لأن شرب الماء الذي في الكوز وقت الحلف ولا ماء فيه لا يتصور فلم تنعقد
He said: (If he swears to ascend the sky or to turn this stone into gold, he breaks the oath immediately.) Zufar said: The oath is not contracted because it is impossible by custom, so it resembles what is impossible in reality. Our proof is that the fulfillment is conceivable in reality — with the kasra on the waw — i.e., possible, because ascending to the sky is possible in reality; do you not see that the angels ascend it? Likewise, the transformation of a stone into gold by Allah's transformation, making the quality of stone into the quality of gold, or by annihilating the parts of stone and replacing them with parts of gold. The transformation in the first is more apparent, and it is possible according to the theologians upon what is correct. And when it is conceivable, the oath is contracted, obligating an oath, then he breaks it by virtue of incapacity established by custom, just as if the swearer dies, he breaks it despite the possibility of restoration of life. And unlike the case of the jug, because drinking the water that was in the jug at the time of swearing when there is no water in it is not conceivable, so it is not contracted.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn and a dispute between the Hanafi school and Zufar regarding oaths to perform acts that are impossible by custom but possible in reality. The Hanafi position is that such oaths are valid and immediately broken. The commentator explains the reasoning: although the act is impossible by human custom (like climbing the sky or turning a stone into gold), it is possible in reality through divine power — angels ascend, and Allah can transform matter. Therefore, the oath is contracted because fulfillment is conceivable (mutasawwar). Once contracted, the oath is broken immediately due to the swearer's customary incapacity to perform the impossible act. This is analogous to a dying person swearing to do something; the oath is valid and broken despite the theoretical possibility of revival. The case differs from the 'kuz' (jug) example, where swearing to drink water from a jug that contains no water at the time of swearing is inconceivable, so the oath is not contracted at all. Zufar's objection based on customary impossibility is rejected because the Hanafis distinguish between real impossibility (which prevents contract) and customary impossibility (which does not).

Key Terms
متصور (mutasawwar): Conceivable or possible in reality, as opposed to being absolutely impossible.
عجز (ajz): Incapacity to perform the sworn act, which leads to immediate breaking of the oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling if someone swears to climb to the sky?
A) The oath is not contracted because it is impossible by custom.
B) The oath is contracted and broken immediately.
C) The oath is valid but only broken after the swearer's death.
D) The oath is suspended until the swearer actually attempts it.

Key Takeaway
Only real impossibility, not customary impossibility, prevents the contract of an oath.
